3422
Period Overlay on Weight Trend
October 19, 2022 at 10:18 PM
Description
We allow basic period tracking on the habits page. In the future we intend to provide more comprehensive analytics for this data, potentially even being able to utilize it for algorithm enhancements.

As a small step in that direction, this feature would bring period data into the weight trend view, to provide more interesting insights in the context of weight trending.

Yes please!! I need to remind myself all the time that my weight has stalled because of my period, it would really help to be able to visualise this. It also means I could get a better idea of what is a “normal” amount of fluctuation to see during my period!

Yes please!!

My weight fluctuates so much depending which stage of my cycle I'm in. Because macrofactor calculates expenditure from the previous weeks' weight fluctuations, I am always left wondering how accurate my expenditure is. For me, I tend to bloat and hold onto weight in the week before my period, then lose that weight during my period (I know everyone is different in this way). This means that macrofactor tends to show that my expenditure decreases in the week before my period and increases during my period even when my exercise and nutrition has otherwise remained unchanged. The app then recommends that I change my calorie intake accordingly, which can be frustrating because I am hungrier the week of my period.

I have still been able to meet my goals with macrofactor and the app has made a massive positive impact in my life. Adding a feature that considers my monthly weight fluctuations in the expenditure calculation would improve my experience with the app significantly. The expenditure calculation is central to the value that macrofactor provides me, so it's important for it to be accurate. Also, I don't know whether women are 50% of macrofactor users, but we are 50% of people and ideally men's bodies would not be the default standard for health and nutrition products.

The main reason I track my period is to predict the date of my next period. I saw that macrofactor incorporated a cycle tracker into its most recent update, which was a promising step! I have been tracking my period with Samsung health because it uses data from my previous periods to project a date for my next period. I can keep tracking my period separately on both apps, but it would be helpful if Macrofactor could incorporate a similar prediction feature so that I could track all of my health data in one place.

Thanks for designing a great app with Macrofactor!! Overall the experience of using the app is miles above any other fitness app I have used. I love and use the ai describe feature, the expenditure calculation, the recipes function, the ad-free design, and just the ease of logging foods and reviewing macros in general. A one-year subscription was easily among hte best purchases I have ever made for my health. Keep up the good work!

Dec 30, 2024, 2:57 PM · 

Yes please!! My weight fluctuates so much during my cycle. Especially right before my period. I end up gaining up to 2kg because my body is preparing for it! Considering how you should also be eating ~200 cals more on your period/right before it since the body uses more energy, it’s kind of discouraging when the calorie deficit ai suggests you should eat less, when in fact it’s going to be counterproductive for people with periods!

I think it would be really useful to have menstrual phase overlay in weight trend and/or energy expenditure!

Jan 5, 2025, 4:57 PM · 

Please add this feature and plan to expand on it in the future, if possible. Personally, the week before, I'll have 2-4 days on intense bottomless pit hunger that nothing seems to satiate, so I'll eat at maintenance and stuff myself with salads and fruits/veggies. That week before I'll also have almost no energy and feel so weak at the gym, it's so frustrating. When I actually start my cycle, when I wake up and do my weight in, I'll have "gained" 2-6lbs overnight just from water weight/bloating. Then when my period ends, the next day (provided I stayed within my defecit) I'll shed 3-9lbs instantly.
It's so frustrating to have to account for this myself because the app sees this and wants to adjust my intake when I need it to chill and wait a week.

2. 3738
Flag Low Quality Branded Product Entries
October 19, 2022 at 10:45 PM
Description
Using some basic checks, we could flag branded product entries that seem like they may be erroneous.

Under Consideration 💭
Comments
--'s avatar
I like the suggestions from the good people above of:
- Suggesting an edit just like in Google Maps.
- Verifying that a food is correct.
- Cross checking the macros against the calories (9g for fat, 4g for carbs & protein). If that’s way off there’s likely something wrong and a food can be flagged.

When generic items (e.g. chicken breast, carrots, shrimp, etc.) are searched for there is no need to see branded items. A chicken breast is a chicken breast unless it is processed in some way (breaded, marinated, etc.) just keep them generic.

I think allowing user corrections is a great idea - I've scanned foods to find they point to the wrong item, nutrients/calories are wrong, or the serving size is missing.

However, the suggestion to not allow users to add items is horrible. It might be fine if you live in maybe the US where MF has an extensive library but if you live in Asia or Europe the database is much sparser.

Jun 12, 2025, 9:49 AM · 
--'s avatar
A very simple sanity check could be to see if the food's kcal entry aligns with its macros. For example, if the food entry claims 5g carbs, 5g protein, and 10g fat per 100g food serving then the kcals/100g should be ~130. Fudge factor around this math should be allowed; MacroFactor could show a yellow "warning" sign if the kcals/serving is more than 20% different from "nominal" energy, and a red "warning" sign if more than 35%. This could very easily and quickly shine a spotlight on problematic entries to avoid.

Jun 26, 2025, 12:38 PM · 
--'s avatar

If I want to eat 1800 calories a day and I want 4 meals and snacks, it shows me the kinds of meals that would meet that target. When I first started, I saw they were much lighter than my intuition told me.

Jun 10, 2025, 11:38 PM · 
--'s avatar
A really basic version of meal planning could be the ability to mark foods in your food log as “uneaten” (exact wording could be something else, eg “planned” or “draft”). These foods would not be summed into the day’s consumed calories and macros etc… they’d only appear in the food log area. This way the food log would serve a dual purpose as a log, and a “future log” aka planning.

Of course, this kind of approach is technically possible right now… but as time passes there’s no easy way to distinguish between foods you’ve actually eaten. Personally I’ve taken to marking planned foods with a specific timestamp (eg “HH:59”), but this feels janky and imperfect, and of course there’s a 1/60 chance I might casually log a food with that same format of timestamp.

Personally this is all I’d really want in terms of meal planning features - combined with the existing recipe library and custom foods i think it might meet a LOT of different needs. I’ve opened a separate more specific feature request for this, but it felt worth mentioning here as well. Thanks for making a great app!

3. Once I hit my daily goal for goal 2, restore goal 1. I am now tracking my trend weight using goal 1.
4. Go to step 2.

It's not great bc I lose how each milestone went, but at least I have a holistic view for the entire program.

Add Negative Calories Macros
October 19, 2022 at 11:24 PM
Description
This feature would allow you to add negative foods for the purposes of subtracting from your daily totals rather than adding to then.

Under Consideration 💭
Comments
--'s avatar
This would be useful for me in ways others have indicated (especially Hello Fresh where I make multiple substitutions/omissions ex: less butter or oil, low cal tortilla, etc). Currently I build out a recipe “my” way or quick add after doing some math but being able to use the pre-entry and just subtract a few things would be sweet.

Jul 3, 2024, 1:05 PM · 
--'s avatar
I agree this would be a very useful feature.

For the first — a placeholder feature for when you’re weighing foods. Enter a “tare/before” value and have the app hold that value until you dish up / eat and re-weigh. Right now I have to jot the number down externally.

For the other, simply having a ± button in the logging keyboard. I would like to see it both on the foods and the “quick add” because then you could leverage the power of the food database for goodish-not-perfect logging.

Didn’t finish your pizza crust? Log the slice and then log a negative partial serving of packaged pre-made pizza crust. Skipped the croutons? Log the salad kit and then log a negative amount of some other random croutons in the food database that you feel is probably comparable.

Loooove it.

Jul 9, 2024, 9:07 PM ·

Apr 30, 10:47 PM · 
--'s avatar
I cooked 5 bone in, skin on chicken thighs for the week using the cold pan method. This is where you lay them skin side down in a cold pan and cook them on the stove top between low and medium low heat. No added oil needed. The fat will slowly render out and yield a nice glassy skin.

When they were finished cooking, there was a probably close to 1/3 cup of rendered fat left in the pan that I did not use, or roughly 68 g of fat and 612 calories over 5 meals.

Protein and carbs are pretty unaffected by cooking, but this happens with fats, so we can’t rely solely on the nutrition facts in some instances.

People have been asking for this feature for almost 4 years…pretty please with protein powder on top.

Under Consideration 💭

I think everyone here agrees the reminder notifications should be OPTIONAL, and preferably OPT IN rather than OPT OUT.

And for those of us who opt in, we want to set reminder notifications at USER-SET TIMES that work for us, times that we can change until we get the right set for ourselves.

For example, 8am, 12pm, 4pm, and 8pm may work for one person, and 10am and 6pm might work for another, and just once a day at 10pm might work for yet another.

I think both types of users would value reminder notifications, albeit in different ways.

Add micronutrient support for iodine
October 19, 2022 at 11:26 PM
Description
Currently iodine isn't a micronutrient that we support because research database coverage of this micronutrient is poor. Maybe it could be helpful to have for custom foods and regions where this may be included on nutrition labels?

Under Consideration 💭
Comments
--'s avatar
In the Nutrition section of the app, I agree it would be very useful if Iodine tracking was included under minerals or other. I have Hashimoto’s thyroiditis and it would be helpful to be able to track and pay attention to my intake. I know that it impacts people with all kinds of thyroid issues. That- Selenium and D3! (Which MF already has) :) Iodine is a trace mineral, which is a type of micronutrient. Trace minerals are essential nutrients that your body requires in very small amounts (hence the term “trace”) to perform critical biological functions. Key Functions of Iodine: • It is primarily required for the production of thyroid hormones (thyroxine [T4] and triiodothyronine [T3]), which regulate metabolism, growth, and development. • It supports thyroid health, preventing conditions like goiter (thyroid gland enlargement) and hypothyroidism. • It plays a role in brain development during pregnancy and early childhood. Despite its small required amount, iodine is crucial for overall health and is considered an essential micronutrient because the body cannot produce it—it must come from the diet. • Recommended Daily Allowance (RDA): • Adults: 150 micrograms (mcg) per day • Pregnant individuals: 220 mcg per day • Lactating individuals: 290 mcg per day • Upper Limit (UL): 1,100 mcg per day (exceeding this could cause thyroid issues). Thanks so much! Love the app so much

Jan 25, 2025, 6:27 AM · 
--'s avatar
What if you had a tooltip which outlined iodine it is not required on nutrition labels in the U.S. therefore estimations were approximate?

And perhaps added some logic for if a good does not have iodine listed in the database, if an entry is in list of iodine related foods then add the approximate amount for the entry. See example below:

1. Seaweed (Best Natural Source)
• Kelp: 2,500 mcg per gram
• Nori (used in sushi): 16–43 mcg per sheet
• Wakame: ~66 mcg per gram
• Dulse: ~72 mcg per gram

2. Iodized Salt
• ~76 mcg of iodine per 1/4 teaspoon (fortified salt is a convenient and controlled source).

3. Seafood

Iodine content is generally high in marine foods:
• Cod: ~99 mcg per 3 oz (excellent source)
• Shrimp: ~35 mcg per 3 oz
• Tuna: ~17 mcg per 3 oz
• Scallops: ~13 mcg per 3 oz
• Oysters: ~160 mcg per 3 oz

4. Dairy Products

Iodine in dairy comes from iodine-rich animal feed and cleaning products:
• Milk: ~85 mcg per 1 cup
• Yogurt: ~75 mcg per 1 cup
• Cheese (cheddar): ~12 mcg per 1 oz

5. Eggs
• ~24 mcg per large egg (mostly in the yolk).


Iodine content in plants depends on the iodine concentration of the soil they’re grown in:
• Potatoes (with skin): ~60 mcg per medium potato
• Cranberries: ~100 mcg per 4 oz (if iodine-rich soil is used)
• Prunes: ~13 mcg per 5 prunes

7. Fortified Plant-Based Alternatives
• Fortified Plant Milks: ~15–56 mcg per cup (check labels for brands adding iodine).
• Fortified Cereals: ~10–50 mcg per serving.

8. Other Foods
• Bread (if made with iodized salt): ~5–30 mcg per slice.
• Legumes (like navy beans): ~32 mcg per 1/2 cup (cooked).
• Seaweed Snacks (packaged): Check labels for iodine levels.

If I try to log 1 cup of navy beans the backend would add ~64 mcg of iodine.

The “” would be fine to indicate appropriate values as well



Jan 25, 2025, 6:42 AM · 
--'s avatar
Would like this

Apr 20, 2025, 9:46 AM ·

Aug 9, 2025, 12:23 PM · 
--'s avatar
The most important thing here is consent and privacy. If this feature gets added, I would like
1. My profile to be invisible to all other users by default. The Finch app lets you add friends by typing in custom codes, and you can only find people by knowing their code. For privacy and control over who you share with, I think this system is excellent.
2. Control over exactly what data which friends could see. Sharing one meal is not consent to see my whole food log. Sharing my food log is not consent to see my weight. Etc.
3. For many people food and weight are deeply personal. Visible share buttons would be very off-putting to me - I would be uncomfortable if my food logging app felt like a social media app. My suggestion is to have share buttons disabled until a person starts adding friends, and perhaps even relegated to a separate screen so they don't appear in the food log or weight tracking portions of the app. I know this is "emotional" but I don't want to be reminded that someone may be watching when I log my food.

Intermittent Fasting Window Indicator
February 15, 2023 at 10:30 AM
Description
This feature would provide you with a timer or another indicator to let you know when you had intended on fasting.

Under Consideration 💭

--'s avatar
Would love if you would also consider adding an automatic calculation for each day to indicate fasting time since last logged intake*.

-- With a settings value for user to input typical length of meal.

-- Available as a dashboard item, and as a widget.

For example, if my last logged intake* timestamp was yesterday at 5:00 pm and I have put in settings that I typically take 30 minutes to eat a meal, if I then look at MacroFactor app the at 9:30 am, it could show me that it's been 16.5 hours since my last meal.

This sort of at-a-glance could be helpful for those who are fasting, and those who need to eat at certain intervals. And could help give us one more easy reminder to log our intake in a timely manner. :0)

* Non-water intake; maybe other exceptions as flagged by system; or could be another user-setting add-on.

--'s avatar
I’d like to second this request. Women’s cycle-related weight fluctuations can be quite significant, and without accounting for them MacroFactor risks over-restricting calories by mistaking water weight for fat gain.

A possible solution could be for the app to analyse months of past weight data (from MacroFactor itself or integrations like Apple Health, Fitbit, Hume, FitTrack, etc.) to identify cyclical patterns. When the cycle toggle is enabled, those fluctuations could be filtered out so the algorithm doesn’t confuse them with genuine weight change.

I love this app. It’s already the best tracker I’ve used hands down, and I think this feature would make it truly unbeatable.

Nov 2, 2024, 12:56 PM · 
--'s avatar
If you're an iOS user, there are some incremental tools for this. A narrow Siri feature "MacroFactor, log beer" will estimate macros based on volume and ABV. It's in beta on TestFlight: http://testflight.apple.com/join/y6egAUKj with some explainers in the app's More menu > Siri.

You can save that Log Beer shortcut with a custom name and fill in some values for simpler dialog (e.g., here is "log a pint").

For other drinks (or beers, too), you could pin a previously logged food or drink in a custom Shortcut. "log a mimosa".

Cheers,

Ryan

Dec 23, 2024, 9:24 PM
· Team member

May 7, 2025, 9:05 AM ·

Yes please!!! DrinkControl is a good app on App Store. Easy for you guys to do this

Jul 2, 2025, 10:38 PM · 
--'s avatar
It only takes a few seconds to calculate this y'all. Say you drink a 44ml shot of 40% abv whiskey. Just multiply the volume by the abv then by the density of alcohol of .789 g/ml. So 44ml * .4 * .789g/ml = 13.89g of alcohol.

Use 'quick add' to add 13.89g alcohol and u get 97 calories.

Itd be nice for this to be built in, but this is how to do it in the meantime. If your cocktail also has sugar then good luck.

Jul 22, 2025, 2:07 AM ·

If the above features were integrated into the app, I’d be happy with that. However, I wouldn’t mind additional features, such as displaying the water logs in the "Food Log" timeline or having the "quick-track" water log buttons appear in the "Favorites" or "Shortcuts & Toolbar" bars, rather than on a separate water tracking page. The possibilities are endless!

Water is definitely worth tracking, but it needs to be quick. I drink lots of small amounts of water throughout the day (as you should), and I need to log it quickly. I don’t want to have to search specifically for water and input a custom amount each time. Right now, I use a separate app for water tracking, which isn’t ideal, but it’s better than nothing. It’s also worth noting that although my water logs appear in Apple Health, they don’t show up in MacroFactor, so I never meet the water goals I’ve set in MacroFactor. Big sad. :(

Thank you so much for listening! I really hope this feature gets added. :) Between this, the new watch and web apps, and the new workout app (which I’m really excited about!), you guys will be covering all my smart-health needs! Keep up the great work, and thank you for creating the best nutrition tracking app ever!

Dec 6, 2024, 2:25 PM · 
--'s avatar
This would be an awesome feature. It’s the only thing I feel this app is really missing. Thanks for considering it.

Cheers,

Ryan

Sep 8, 2025, 11:38 PM · 
--'s avatar
+10000000000. Most important feature missing.

Currently fiber is grouped together with carbohydrates for all purposes in the app, as per the USA standard. However, most of the countries in the world - countries in European Union, Australia, New Zealand, United Kingdom, countries in Asia – list fiber separately from carbohydrates. That is because fiber is not absorbed in the small intestine, provides minimal energy and serves a different function than digestable carbs. There needs to be an option to select to display carbohydrates separately from fiber - to display available carbohydrates in place of carbohydrates - because:

1. The carbohydrate macro displayed stops making sense outside of USA. My target for carbohydrates is listed as 156gr per day in the app, I ate 300 gr. of white beans. The app displays that for the day I have consumed 186.9 grams of carbohydrates. While based on EU labeling, I have consumed 132.6 grams of carbohydrates and 54.3 grams of fiber. The macro target just doesn’t really make sense if you live outside of the USA. Also, likely doesn’t make much sense in the USA, fiber is labeled aside from carbohydrates because it serves a different function than available/digestable carbohydrates and is much more nutritionally inert. It doesn’t make that much sense to have a macronutrient target for carbohydrates if the categories of carbohydrates are severely different, such as available/digestable carbohydrates and fiber, as they have different nutritional values, so any such target becomes essentially meaningless, because you may eat 156 grams of fiber or 156 grams of available carbohydrates and they will have severely different calorie values and also nutritional impact of how the body processes them.
2. I live in EU, all food nutrition labels display carbohydrates separately from fiber (as many other countries across the world do). Most of the food (including general foods!) in macrofactor database differs from what I see on the nutrition labels. That is greatly confusing, annoying and makes the food database largely unusable.


Therefore, please make an option to select so that available carbohydrates would be displayed in place of carbohydrates in all places through the app. And that then when one is adding food, just based on this option selection, all available foods in the database would also separate fiber from carbohydrates (available carbohydrates).

Otherwise, please clearly state this for potential users. I wouldn’t have subscribed if I knew the app was so American-centric and hasn’t been adopted for the rest of the world even in the most basic features, such as macros, which are in the name of the app.

--'s avatar
Yes this would be huge. One mistake i often see with nutrition tracking web interfaces, is the UI/UX requires both mouse and keyboard to fully enter information. Type name, weight, etc but then if hit enter often just closes and then have to use mouse to click the 'add' button. Benefit of keyboard ability is once you start entering you should be able to add multiple items without having to lift up your hands from the keyboard. Often aided with different actions bound to Tab, Return, Shift+Tab, Shift+Return, etc. MyNetDiary's webinterface does this well. A few others.

Iphone is good if you add as you go, but if you slip and have to enter 1 or 2 days info at once its pretty tedious. with pure keyboard entry its trivial.

--'s avatar
Before our Apple Watch app arrives, a minor feature:
You can see your the rest timer (+ get optional nudges as and after the rest ends) on your Watch’s Smart Stack with our iPhone Live Activity feature.

A beta is in TestFlight now (https://testflight.apple.com/join/Uu1wtQeW). The feature will be in App Store release 1.2.0.

Feedback: Live Activity feature channel or support@macrofactorapp.com

Tips

The”Smart Stack” is what appears on your watch face when scrolling the crown.

It may take a few seconds for your iPhone to update the Watch, but the rest timer that appears will be accurate.

Add Micronutrients to Custom Foods using %DV
September 18, 2024 at 01:01 PM
Description
The latest nutrition label reduces the utility of this idea. Using the amount rather than the percent should be more convenient and accurate.

https://www.fda.gov/food/food-labeling-nutrition/changes-nutrition-facts-label

Won't Do ⛔
#Out of Scope 📲
Comments
--'s avatar
I'd argue this should be reconsidered. The exact amounts are listed only for Vitamin D, Calcium, Iron, and Potassium. If a label lists other nutrients they are usually only listed as a %DV. That means we'd have to look up what that translates to ourselves, or more likely, just skip adding that nutrient to custom foods altogether.

For example, the Vitamin A field has a drop-down to allow it to be entered in mcg or IU. I don't know why there can't be a third %DV option where I can enter 15% when that's all I see on the label, and the app can do the conversion for me, in this case that 15% DV on a US label that assumes a 2000 calorie diet means 135mcg.

What the DV is assumed to be on USA labels is documented here. There's no way I'm going to open this page and calculate it myself for each nutrient when entering custom foods, I'm just going to skip them.

https://www.fda.gov/food/nutrition-facts-label/daily-value-nutrition-and-supplement-facts-labels

Oct 28, 2024, 10:00 AM · 
--'s avatar
^ agree with the comment above on would like to see %DV added as a unit of measure for recording vitamins

Oct 30, 2024, 11:35 AM · 
--'s avatar
If I’m creating a food that hasn’t been scanned I’m already in somewhat of a rush. Needing to manually calculate the dv% when this is a standard and known formula is silly, and not having it feels the same as if the app only supported stone and deciliters and said “well you can do the math in your head, it’s easy”

Mar 4, 2025, 1:17 PM · 
--'s avatar
Agreed with the above. The actual weight or volume of the specific nutritional elements isn't always given but rather shown as a percent of daily value. I believe those Baseline numbers are US Standard for the calorie daily value. If that were used to calculate against a percentage given for a percent DV, then a volume could be added. That shouldn't be a very difficult thing to implement just using a look up table against the percentage when adding values in percent

If anything, wouldn't logging calorie burn help confirm that your algorithms are actually working?

--'s avatar
This suggestion is unscientific. Doing 500 cals of cardio does not automatically mean your deficit is 500 calories bigger that day. Most people compensate by walking and fidgeting less later in the day. Plus, there is no remotely accurate way of knowing how many calories you burned doing any activity - fitness watches can't actually know this.

Wearable Integrations (Fitbit, Garmin, Oura, Whoop, ...)
September 18, 2024 at 12:33 PM
Description
Integrations
Our integration strategy is to support Health Connect on Android, and Apple Health on iOS.

For their respective operating systems, these are the secure on-device health management platforms through which almost all other integrations should connect.

Our integration with these platforms is likely to serve as an indirect integration with your favorite platform.

On Android, our integration will also serve as a direct integration with Google Fit, Fitbit, and Samsung Health.

Wearables
If you're looking to integrate your wearable for the activity data, that's not something our algorithms utilize, and for good reason. https://macrofactorapp.com/wearables/

Won't Do ⛔
#Out of Scope 📲

Jan 16, 5:46 PM · 
--'s avatar
Exporting the workout routines/programs to platforms like Garmin, Apple Health/Workouts, and Google Fit, to be used on smartwatches (and avoid having to be forced to use your phone while working out), is entirely possible.

For example, I use Garmin and via their Training API it would allow you to submit workout programs so that users can see them on their Garmin watches: https://developerportal.garmin.com/developer-programs/connect-developer-api

For now, I am solving the issue for myself by using some AI and a Garmin MCP, I added the ability to create workouts so I was able to convert your xslx file to csv, and then pass it on to an AI model to use this feature (https://github.com/velazcod/garmy/commit/5f4b120bdc1c63b2f9b4324a3867d36b518faaed) to add it to my Garmin account. I worked on a fuzzy exercise name matching feature to ensure the names match the way Garmin expects them, you are welcome to get inspiration from it. But this is currently not a real solution for most users since it's an advanced way of doing it.

Smart Progression Weight Recommendation Improvement
January 13, 2026 at 02:24 PM
Description
We're designing a system to heavily reduce the number of occasions where smart progression inserts a weight into the weight text field that isn't supported by your gym profile.

This happens when no valid combination of your target rep range, target RIR, and available gym weight for an exercise can be found to satisfy your predicted performance for a specific set.

Currently, this scenario requires you to use the "fixes" system to apply a rep range adjustment or gym weight adjustment.

With the new system that you can opt out of should you choose, we will flexibly adjust your target rep range as needed to resolve this scenario automatically.

Released
Comments

Mar 28, 12:25 PM · 
--'s avatar
Our Live Activity is available for beta testing: https://testflight.apple.com/join/Uu1wtQeW

See your current set or rest on your Lock Screen and Dynamic Island

Optional nudges when a rest finishes, plus follow-up reminders if you get distracted

Feedback: support@macrofactorapp.com


Live Activity tips

Next button logs the set as-is

Tap weight/reps/etc to quickly edit in the app

Tap the thumbnail to open the exercise video

Back button "unchecks" the set

A small read-only version appears in your paired Watch’s Smart Stack. It can take a beat to update, but is handy for seeing your rest timer countdown.

Open questions

Should the post-tap update animation be more subtle? The wait would still remain.

In the app, swiping between exercises changes the “current set” shown in the Live Activity — is that sometimes undesirable?

Is the “Up Next” snippet at the bottom of the Live Activity helpful, or does it feel out of place?

Mar 30, 2:32 PM
· Team member
--'s avatar
Beta 2 is now available (replacing Beta 1) with new options (auto-next after rest timer hits zero) and bug fixes (e.g., ending a workout could spawn another workout).

Please send feedback in app via More tab > Support > Submit Bug Report. Most TestFlight screens are anonymous, which means we cannot ask questions to flesh out what went wrong.

Cheers,
Ryan

Workout App
September 18, 2024 at 12:44 PM
Description
It’s official. We are building a workout app!

Much like the nutrition app, the workout app will feature an easy-to-use interface, helpful analytics, evidence-based recommendations, and innovative and meticulously crafted utilities.

We can’t give too many details on this new app yet, but we can let you know that development has already begun, and we are all extremely excited about what we’re cooking up for you.

Released

Dec 7, 2025, 10:23 AM · 
--'s avatar
Long-time subscriber here (going on 4 years!) and super pumped for the Workouts app. I wanted to share a feature idea I think could genuinely push MacroFactor into a league of its own, and I’d love to hear what the community and dev team think.

One thing that would be incredible for the upcoming MacroFactor Workouts app is the ability to sync with WHOOP(or other recovery trackers) to guide training stress and volume based on actual recovery and strain data.
Imagine this:
Your WHOOP Recovery Score influences that day’s training load
HRV trends automatically adjust intensity recommendations
Sleep + strain data suggest when to push harder or when to pull back
MacroFactor uses all this alongside nutrition data for a full ecosystem
Autoregulated training that adapts to you, not the other way around
As someone who uses both WHOOP and MacroFactor daily — and tracks consistently — I think this integration could create the smartest feedback loop in fitness:
Nutrition → Recovery → Training → Progression → Back to Nutrition
A full circle system instead of disconnected data points.
MacroFactor already nails accuracy and user agency on the nutrition side. Adding recovery-informed programming would make the Workout app the most intelligent and personalized training tool out there.
I know integrations can be complex, but even a simple “Recovery Score → Suggested Training Stress” model would be game-changing.
Would love to know:
Do other users want something like this?
Mods/devs: Is this something that could be on the long-term roadmap?
Anyone else using WHOOP with MF — how do you imagine this working?
Really excited for January 2026 and everything the MF team is building.
Huge respect for the transparency, science-first approach, and the quality of the app so far.

Apple Watch support + complication

Aug 9, 2025, 8:41 PM · 
--'s avatar
If you're interested in beta testing our Apple Watch app, we've opened up more seats today as we do more QC.

(We've been lucky to have a bunch of helpful beta testers this summer who have fixed bugs and flagged great feature ideas. Thank you!!)

To join, open this TestFlight on iPhone: https://testflight.apple.com/join/y6egAUKj. To have it appear on your Watch: in Apple's iPhone TestFlight app, you may need to scroll down to the "Install on Watch" toggle. While we try to keep the App Store iPhone app in sync with these TestFlights, releases might get cut in a way where sometimes the TestFlight is behind or ahead. You should be able to hop on and off without losing data.

When you hit snags, please shout out to support@macrofactorapp.com (or use the iPhone app support button) and flag "Apple Watch". That'll help loop in the right devs, facilitate some back-and-forth to resolve your issues, and give us some account context for debugging.

We'd also enjoy hearing what you find valuable in the beta, as that helps us prioritize where to iterate and improve. For example, there may be some features that you found useful, but weren't very obvious (e.g., you can speed up logging multiple things at once by swiping food rows and swiping up on most white logging buttons). That feedback can help us up our game. :)

Heads up to watchOS 26 users: you can edit our nutrition complications and should see some glass where appropriate. We are tracking an issue with Apple where clock avoidance no longer works as in watchOS 11.

Cheers,
Ryan

In-app Subscription Management
October 19, 2022 at 10:20 PM
Description
This feature will allow users to manage their subscriptions in-app. This would allow trial users and active subscription users on Android to alter the length of their selected subscription. This feature is available through the app store on iOS, but not on Android.

This screen will show the active subscription, and pricing for all alternatives as well.

Released
